#  [](/thread/22510-eagle-method-ma-crossover-system)Eagle Method MA Crossover System 

  * 

  * [#1](/thread/22510-eagle-method-ma-crossover-system "Post Permalink")

  * First Post: Edited 7:09pm  Mar 27, 2007 8:57am | Edited 7:09pm 

  * [ tbwss1234](tbwss1234)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: eaglewoodbury | [77 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35418)

Hi Guys.  
  
I've been trading for quite a while mainly news. But i have been working on an extremely simple but powerful trading system, based on Crossovers here it goes...  
  
Pairs  
Any.. but i use the GBP/JPY  
  
Time frame  
30min-1hr  
  
Indicators  
9 SMA on close  
100 SMA on close  
RVI = 100 (relative vigor index) same as Sidus' indicator. (THIS INDICATOR IS NOT NECESSARY I USE IT FOR MOMENTUM MAINLY)   
  
Method  
LONG - When the 9 crosses above the 100 SMA Buy and it helps if the RVI is above 0  
SHORT - When the 9 crosses below the 100 SMA Sell and it helps if the RVI is below 0  
  
(EXIT)  
Close your position and reverse it when the 9 crosses back or Close the position when the price crosses back over the 9 SMA by 20 pips.  
  
Money Management.  
I found an awesome Excel file that calculates your MM for you. I'll post it up today or tomorrow with a chart for the system.  
  
Additions  
You may generally have periods when the price may whipsaw 1 or 2 times in a row, but 80-90% of the time when the 9 crosses the 100 you will catch an awesome move.. I trade only the GBP/JPY on the 1 hour (1 to 2 trades a week)  
  
Let's get together and run this system to see how it goes. I have noticed on occasion you may miss pips waiting for it to cross back. So maybe we can implement a trailing stop. And let's look at an EA maybe.  
  
Also , NO fibs or pivots.. Not necessary for this method. 

  * [#2](/thread/post/254572#post254572 "Post Permalink")

  * [ tbwss1234](tbwss1234)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: eaglewoodbury | [77 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35418)

Even though it is essentially a crossover system.. The 9 - 100 is a large enough deviation to avoid Ranging and Whipsaws.. Just look at the 1 HOUR CHART on the GBP/JPY it will surprise you.

  * [#11](/thread/post/254687#post254687 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 27, 2007 12:00pm  Mar 27, 2007 12:00pm 

  * [ tbwss1234](tbwss1234)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: eaglewoodbury | [77 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35418)

I'll revise the exit options for you tonight in more detail.  
  
But this is the basic rundown i use.  
  
1\. Either exit on MA's crossing back  
2\. TP of 200  
3\. Exit when price retraces and closes above or below the 9 SMA.. and has at least 20 pips distance between the open and close.

  * [#17](/thread/post/254725#post254725 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 27, 2007 12:59pm  Mar 27, 2007 12:59pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar18555_4.gif) jest1081](jest1081)

  * Joined Sep 2006 | Status: Chasing Trends | [2,339 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18555)

weel one things for sure...there i no perfect system...this one will fail on choppy days. But for whats worth, we want to make it a winning one. like you said there are a few ways to make the exit better. I have a few ideas.   
  
\- 1 use 21sma Open and Close tunnel. This was once used by twoblink on 55ema open close tunnel i think it works well. TP on tunnel cross.   
  
\- Incremental tp, 50, 70, 100 followed by trail. This will be discretional.   
  
I would not tweak too much from there on. You already have something good going here.

Here is an example of the power of using the RVI indicator to filter out ranging/Choppy markets..  
  
Two no trades then one sell for i think 200 pips profit in the end.  
  
So the RVI mostly protects you but on a rare occasion the RVI may cause you to enter late. But it can be worth it.

> 
> Ignored

The RVI will give you a confirmation of momentum.. So when it is below Zero It means we are most probably in for a solid move.  
  
I usually take all of the crosses then watch the RVI and make sure it heads past the Zero.. If it doesn't then i may implement a TP or Even close the position.  
  
Remember your success will come, when you learn to surf the market like a wave.. and work out the patterns that make that wave worth riding.   
  
I suggest entering all the crossovers then using discretionary factors to determine when to exit. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#76](/thread/post/255940#post255940 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 28, 2007 6:39pm  Mar 28, 2007 6:39pm 

  * [ Nybegynner](nybegynner)

  * | Joined Jun 2006  | Status: Trader | [75 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=12543)

The problem here is that you need a solid exit method. If you dont have a solid exit method backtesting this is useless.   
  
Exiting when the ma crosses back over will totaly kill you in a range bound market. Take a look at eg june last year.  
  
So the problem will be, when to take a few pips, and when to let it ride. The fact that it works awsomely well now, does not mean it wont kill your account as soon as you have a ranging market. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

The RVI's and MA's protect your entry when the market is rangebound.. And that's why this thread has been set up to define a good exit.. You can still profit from whipsaws if you have a solid exit strategy..  
  
Maybe a trailing stop may work.. Guys we need to consolidate our brains and work on this..  
  
And regarding backtesting.. I don't think you can ever apply it to any real system.. Because it's pretty much a known fact by pro traders that a purely mechanical system won't work for exits ever.. It takes the trader as the individual to watch the market move and determine his moves based on price activity  
  
We have a system here that will give you awesome entries.. Again, let's get together and work out the best exit, even if it means expressing some key points on how to observe the price...

  * [#82](/thread/post/255992#post255992 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 28, 2007 7:39pm  Mar 28, 2007 7:39pm 

  * [ tbwss1234](tbwss1234)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: eaglewoodbury | [77 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35418)

Hey there.. And your comments are justified and important as it keeps momentum going in this thread.. And criticism is great so keep up the quesiotns ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) .  
  
Generally when the market is ranging.. and you get a buy signal.. The RVI won't be above zero.. This happens most of the time in a ranging market.. And if you notice the 9 SMA and 100SMA is a filter based on their distance between eachother alone.. If you look back you can still make 20 - 50 pips when during whippy times.. So what we need to do is aim to develop sound money management.  
  
so within the month if you grab a large move.. then aim for smaller moves for the rest of the month..  
  
with 100 pips a week you have the potential to turn 1000k into 100 000 in a short time..   
  
And without stops you can avoid a lot of stop hunting done by the retail brokers.  
  
If you look back their is an EXCEL file called trading plan.. It is great for showing how you can grow your account..

  * [#83](/thread/post/256010#post256010 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 28, 2007 8:11pm  Mar 28, 2007 8:11pm 

  * [ peterdxb](peterdxb)

  * | Joined Feb 2006  | Status: Trader | [239 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=6100)

how bout exits in this way:   
  
example:   
1\. 30min SELL trade signal (this is our first trade) then,  
2\. 5min there is 9sma&100sma crossup, we can exit the trade.  
3\. if 5min we get 9/100 crossdown, we SELL again.  
4\. if 5min we get 9/100 crossup, we exit SELL, next if 15min also we get crossup, then we wait for 15min crossdown to re-enter SELL trade (avoid 5min crossdown as it will come before 15min crossdown)  
  
5\. this way we dont have to wait for 9/100crossup on 30min chart to exit position, and we could save some pips.  
  
PS: for 5min and 15min chart same setup as 30min chart and same rules for entries   
  
just an idea ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

So what we need to do is aim to develop sound money management.

  * Edited 11:51pm  Mar 28, 2007 11:37pm | Edited 11:51pm 

  * [ peterdxb](peterdxb)

  * | Joined Feb 2006  | Status: Trader | [239 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=6100)

Here is a chart of 8th FEB, SELL traded loss of 100pips (whipsaw) if profits not locked or improper stops prior to CrossUP on 30min chart.  
  
But i checked it again as per the exit rules i mentioned in previous post, loss on the same signal would have been less then 20pips ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1).  
  
1\. CrossDOWN on 30min chart SELL @ 237.13  
2\. CrossUP on 5min chart , so we Exit SELL @ 237.20  
3\. CrossUP on 15min chart  
3\. CrossDown on 15min chart, so re-entry SELL @ 236.62  
4\. CrossUP on 5min chart so Exit SELL @ 236.73 

Attached Image

  * [#99](/thread/post/256344#post256344 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 29, 2007 12:28am  Mar 29, 2007 12:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar12419_4.gif) StoragePro](storagepro)

  * Joined Jun 2006 | Status: Vivere! | [1,034 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=12419)

This kind of MA based solution works nicely in a trending market - and FX is the trendingest (a real word?) market there is. The difficulty is detecting a ranging market. Ranging is only recognized as it clips you. Then you can build a strategy for taking adavantage of it. Box Plays come to mind.  
  
RVI is a help - I would suggest going back and applying some basic Technical Analysis on price action to help detirmine entry and exit points. Pivots would be a help too. Daily, Weekly and Monthly. Confluence of S/R lines are like solid walls very often and indicate a great exit point.  
  
Plain old indicators gets you part way there.  
  
Multi Timeframes is likewise an excellent thing to observe. I personally like to trade *with* the larger trend as it results in higher probability trades. MA's, Stoch's, MACD, etc - pick your poison.  
  
In all - you'll never catch every trade. You'll never win every one. You can learn to recognize one that is not working out. Discipline will enable you to get out of it before you get completely smashed.  
  
Last thought - I really like scaling into a trade. Start with a toe in the water, and then scale in as it goes your way. Scale out as milestones are hit - pivots or touching a previous swing high/low for example. In this way, our pain is minimized in a bad trade, and you are consistently ringing the cash register on the way up.  
  
Anyone notice that this kind of trading works kind of nice on a daily chart too? After a nice trend, I see that we tend to see a period of consolidation. Either play this as a box play or find a different instrument. Something is always on the move. 

I'm pretty much done with all this ...

  * | Joined Mar 2005  | Status: Trader | [228 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=2118)

Str8,  
I've been F12ving through the years checking out the way Price interactes with the Channels you suggested.   
  
If you only trade crosses where price exceeded the channel on the previous move it does indeed avoid the Whip.   
  
Although extreem there only appears to be a couple periods of Whip with this MA Combination and they seem to happen in groups. (Maybe once or twice a year)   
  
Would it make sense to take all crosses regardles of price exceeding the Channel until a loss? After the first Loss wait for Price to exceed the Channel for a "Perfect Setup". (Similar to 4hour tunnel and Vegas rules)  
  
Looking at several months of data, several profitable trades whould have been missed waiting for the "Perfect Setup".   
  
I'll try to do a manual Backtest of 2 years to see what the numbers look like.  
  
Either way I'm really excited about this system and the additions you have provided.  
  
Joe

It goes like this.  
  
ASIA. in the first hour of activity it will either create a range of trend.. If it ranges Europe will break out and so on.. It always happens this way..

I've met quite a few pro traders in my time and you would be shocked to know how simple their methods are.. It's all about UNDERSTANDING the patterns of the price activity

> Disliked

> All of what you are saying is oh so wonderful.. But as a beginner you need to understand that any trading system is discretionary.. So for example if sometimes you FEEL like the RVI isn't necessary don't use it. And when you understand the patterns of the market you will be able to see DURING ASIA that it is ranging etc..  
>    
>  Haha and mate, look at the EXCEL sheet properly you set you own risk model.. It can be 1% or 100%... read it properly..

>  NO system is going to win 100% of the time.. And their is no such thing as MECHANICAL.. You need to apply your own decisions.. SO if you see a market ranging get out..  
>    
>  And as i said when it is whipsawing make smaller profits..

>  So i suggest either you start paper trading this system and seeing how powerful it is, and using your DISCRETION to exit.. Or try something else..

> 
> Ignored

  
Ok, so you dont have any solid rules for knowing when to stay in the market or not. If you dont see how you would have lost a buch of pips with the exit you sugested, then you better backtest again.   
  
"the system protects you" is true only to a certian degree, cause the RVI as you use it will keep you out of quite a few of the good trades as well (like yesterday's sell) so if you don't have any rules for when to use it or not, then you might as well just skip it. In fact you dont even have a system yet, just a framework to build a sytem on. Sure you can trade mechanical, just not with the 1000+% a year that most of the people in here dream about.  
  
I have backtested this system with stocks, histstepstock, rvi, rsi today, and nothing of it will tell you not to enter and get whiped. You can reduce the whipping with 40/50% though. I actually found HistStepStock to be a better filter than RVI.  
  
Most people in here dont realise that if they make 100% in a year, that is VERY good ROI.

  * Mar 29, 2007 8:28am  Mar 29, 2007 8:28am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar33510_4.gif) TradeStar](tradestar)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: Trader | [476 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=33510)

One other suggestion on entry:  
  
For Long Entry:  
  
1) 9 Ma crosses 100 (Original condition)  
  
AND   
  
2) Order is placed few pips above the high of the first candle that actually closed above the 100 sma  
  
This way you can even place an entry order in advance.  
  
  
The reverse applies for Short entry.  
  
This can reduce the whipsaws to a great extent.  
  
\- RH

> 
> Disliked
> 
>   
>  Would it make sense to take all crosses regardles of price exceeding the Channel until a loss? After the first Loss wait for Price to exceed the Channel for a "Perfect Setup". (Similar to 4hour tunnel and Vegas rules)  
>    
>  Looking at several months of data, several profitable trades whould have been missed waiting for the "Perfect Setup".   
>    
>    
>  Joe
> 
> Ignored

  
At the end of the day, it's all about risk tolerance.  
  
To me, I would rather have fewer losing trades, and end up missing some of the moves, than to keep trading until I hit a loss. It's actually kind of empowering to be on the sidelines during a big move that didn't fit your rules. It means you did the right thing.  
  
There will always be another trade/trend. You're never going to hit all the good ones, but why not just take the higher probability setups? 

Follow my advice at your own peril....

Hi, I have a suggestion for exit.   
I tried adding CCI 14. How it works?  
  
Firstly,   
  
During entry,make sure when MA9 crosses MA100,   
  
**Long, CCI is above 0  
Short, CCI is below zero**  
  
THEN,  
  
**EXIT, wait for CCI goes back to 0...**  
  
my english sucks so plz see the picture for a clearer view thanx.  
  
Do you think adding SHI channel will do any good?For example if a cross happens(LONG) near the top of the channel, it can make a u turn...**Correct me if I'm wrong**

  * [#155](/thread/post/257788#post257788 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 30, 2007 3:09am  Mar 30, 2007 3:09am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar10489_4.gif) ahendon](ahendon)

  * | Joined May 2006  | Status: Sharing Transformation | [41 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=10489)

I have been trying something using a 4hr charts for a bunch of reasons - I don't want to hang around and watch the screen all night, I want to eliminate the whips, I think longer term is more stable and profitable, etc... so in playing with the set ups I found something interesting in regards to the exits (which is the problem we are out to solve, yes?). Well check this out:  
  
If you set the period in the RVI to 1 on a 4hr chart something interesting happens. If you enter at a cross and stay in until the RVI line crosses 0 in the opposite direction and exit (not reverse, just exit and chill) and wait until it either crosses back (trend resumes) or it leads to a MA cross (reverse) you eliminate much loss of pipage.  
  
There is for sure discretion involved in this (as we have established there is in everything) and I am just starting to test it but it was too cool not share.  
  
check it out for yourself. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#157](/thread/post/257845#post257845 "Post Permalink")

  * Mar 30, 2007 4:13am  Mar 30, 2007 4:13am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar10489_4.gif) ahendon](ahendon)

  * | Joined May 2006  | Status: Sharing Transformation | [41 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=10489)

I don't know how to paste a screen shot but here is how you change the RVI to 1:  
  
assuming you already have the indicator attached just right click on it and select: INDICATOR LIST. Then highlight the RVI indicator and select EDIT. Then in the parameters tab simple change the period from 10 (or whatever it is) to 1 and select OK.  
  
that's it. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#158](/thread/post/257873#post257873 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 5:07am  Mar 30, 2007 4:43am | Edited 5:07am 

  * [ fritz](fritz)

  * | Joined Jul 2004  | Status: Trader | [75 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=665)

One of the best filters you can use in trading this method and many others is "to wait". When the ma's cross simply wait and watch how price reacts, then make your decision. Using waiting as a filter you will miss some of the move but your emotions will be minimized. For example when the ma's cross let price take off and then it will bounce/pullback, sometimes a little and sometimes alot, when it does that take a look at the highest high for buys and lowest lows for sells and put in a pending order 10-50 pips away from those price areas. With a pending order ie. buy stops and sell stops you are choosing the General direction of the trade but at the end of the day you are allowing price to choose the Specific direction when price moves and opens your position for you. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

>  I agree with your method. I also believe that the price action creates a pattern I like to place my order entry (10 pips away). And when I got fillled, I manage my trade by moving my stop loss until the price kicks me out. Check my pictures.  
>    
>  Regards,  
>  Rick
> 
> Ignored

Great to see you guys are thinking about the system and personalizing your own method. Trailing stops and order stops can definately work...   
  
Hope you all entered the last signal.. That's two in a row ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f60a.png?v=15.1) Remember i don't ALWAYS follow the RVI.. When it does give us a perfect signal.. It most probably will give us a nice run.. But i most often enter all crosses..   
  
I watch the signals that weren't a perfect set up, just in case it reverses.. And let the perfect set up run.  
  
I also am trialing moving a stop to Break even at 50 pips

On the guppy, I've been watching for the 9/100 SMA cross on the 15M chart, wait for confirmation of a cross on the 30M, and enter on the open of the next candle. My last entry was at 230.73 on the 12:00 GMT candle, and I closed at 231.73 for +100 pips. I'm considering using a large trail of 50 pips, setting BE at 50, or scaling out at either fibs or set targets (ex. 25, 50, 75, etc).   
  
The entry seems to be the easy part...finding the optimum exit might take a bit (which is true for all methods, right ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f609.png?v=15.1)

When you enter the trade.. Try looking at the smaller timeframes to exit...  
  
So when the 9 crosses back over the 100SMA in the 15 min or 5min exit the position.. And re-enter if it crosses back down  
  
or  
  
I am also looking at the 125 -125 pip channel posting in this thread.. as an initial exit.. If it bounces at that point i exit and wait for it to break past.. then re-enter.

Hi str8deals thanks for you fantastic suggestion..  
  
I have implemented it and am using it.. It has been working on the 30 min as well for the GBP/JPY...  
  
What i am doing now is  
  
1\. ENTER ON CROSS  
2\. CHECK RVI if it's past zero then it will be a nice move and i can let it run.. If it isn't past ZERO then i watch the trade carefully  
3\. I wait for the price to hit the outer channel (125) then I move to the 5 min TF.. If it retraces by 30 pips i exit the trade.. If it passes the channel i then...  
4\. Hold the position and implement a 50 pip trailing stop..

  * [ ssotiro](ssotiro)

  * | Joined Sep 2006  | Status: Trader | [271 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=18302)

Hi,  
When you want to draw an MA on the chart, you have to chose the period, the "MA method" (Exponential, simple etc) and the "Apply to" tab.  
  
In our case, you have to chose "Apply to: close".  
  
Hope this helps

I was backtesting this using the straight cross of the 9 over the 100 and in trying to figure an exit method that would not lose as many pips as simply waiting for a re-cross, and therefore a reversal, I applied fractals and used them as a trailing stop. It was pretty successful. I also found that not applying a stop initially was the best method to get the trade going, however, I could not trade this way live. So I would have to figure some emergency stop loss number to apply initailly in the trade.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar16397_4.gif) droesparky](droesparky)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [149 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=16397)

here is a idea for a better exit. It will vary a little from broker to broker but should be close enough.  
  
Draw trend lines as the run is moving keep updating the trend lines. when price breaks or closes (closes) the trend line exit the trade. It could also give you a heads up on the next entry. but I would move stop to be on the trendline break as soon as possible. there is some discretion to it.  
  
do some backtesting this weekend while moving one cadle at a time.  
  
Mouteki method has some great lessons on drawing trend lines.   
  
Its as simple as this method and seeems to work well with it for exits.  
  
Youll never get every pip, just like youll always have loosing trades.  
  
here is the recent chart with a few lines on it. You can see how it would get you out long before a cross happens. Most of the time you have a trendline in place before the cross that gets you into a trade. this could also help with, getting out early on whips?  
  
Needs some backtest but I think you can see it can work and it simple. 

Attached Image

![](/attachment/image/27409?d=1175289846)

I got into the gbp/jpy yesterday afternoon...1 minute I was up 28 pips with a 50 pip stop loss...then I saw it going down on some news so I got rid of the stop loss and let it ride down.   
  
It went down 120 pips then hovered around the 50 pip in the minus for me...then this morning it was all over the place and I got out with 9 pip profit (real money) just before the close of the day....I didn't want to be in over the weekend and see a big spike to the down side on the open on sunday.  
  
But great system.....I think I will be able to make some money out of this one.

Good for you Billser for getting out of that one positive. Backtesting this shows it will hurt bad during a ranging market, as we all know ma cross systems do. It will reward nicely though in a trend, again this is not news to most of us. I don't think this is any better or any worse than other ma crossover systems. Money management will save you with it. If you can weather the range periods then you should make money in capturing the trends.

  * [#196](/thread/post/259473#post259473 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 1, 2007 11:50am  Apr 1, 2007 11:50am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar16397_4.gif) droesparky](droesparky)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [149 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=16397)

Well Ive bee trying to nail down the exit strat by using trendlines and I found that I would end up exiting early most of the time. perhaps I just need more practice with trendlines. There is a indicator out there that will draw the latest trendlines for you. Demark_trend_alert_and_mail it will alert you when price crosses the lines. Im not on my home ccomputor or I would atach it.  
  
I also added a 05 and -.05 level to the RVI set to 100 period, and found that once the RVI is past those levels and crosses back that is a good time to exit the trade. I would like some of you to test this also and see what you think of it for a exit strat.The 125 channels work great and if price has been outside of them and comes back in it is at least a warning that things are cooling down, but the RVI tells even more. I had never used the RVI before but like it much better then other oscillators.  
  
I also tried a old idea that I was thaught by Rob Booker. We all know the trend is our friend but determining the trend is what we struggle with. Rob used the 62 to tell him the trend in his 5/13/62 method. The Idea is to use a higher ma, which is in turn using a higher time frame to show the trend.  
  
I decided to try putting a 200 ma on the chart and which ever side of the 200 the 100 is on thats the safest direction to trade. So if the 100 is below the 200 you take short trades. this will keep you out of most of the whips. Even when the 100 is flat if the 200 is coming down you sill would look for short trades. when both 200 and 100 are flat and close to eacch other its time to be careful or look for another pair to trade. Im also checking it with the 144sma but so far like the 200 best.  
  
I also added a P-sar and noticed that when the dots change your safe to get out and when it goes back in your diretion your safe to get back in, as long as the 9 has not crossed the 100. However it will change back and forthe several times in a good run.  
  
BTW this seems to work on all TFs also. Remembe it will work on other pairs so it things flatten out try check another pair for a while. Hope this helps.  
  
I would like a indicator to tell me the distance between two MAs and if they are moving closer or farther apart. Is there anything like that out there?  
  
Thanks tbwss1234 I really like this system!

  * [ Kevinc3po](kevinc3po)

  * | Joined Apr 2007  | Status: Trader | [3 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=36455)

> [Quoting chrisbedo](/thread/post/258920#post258920 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Try just adding a 21 ema and taking the cross for the exit. A shorter EMA might work better but the 21 is pretty good.
> 
> Ignored

  
This along the lines of what I`m thinking.  
  
First enter with 2 positions as the 9 MA crosses the 100 MA.  
  
Exit one position when the 9 MA crosses the 20 MA opposite to the trend. (or 21 in your case)  
  
Re-enter anytime the 9 crosses the 20 going WITH the overall position.  
  
Exit first (overall) position only when the 9 re crosses the 100 line.  
  
  
This way your sealing in some profits everytime the 9 crosses the 20 but you keep one position in for the entire move.  
  
The second position is more like a long term scalping move but insures you keep more profit if the bigger move goes against you for a smaller profit.  
  
Haven`t tested it out yet but I`ll try it tomorrow.  
  
First post on this forum but I love this method so far. Looks like easy money ! (easier the better IMO)

>  What i am doing now is  
>    
>  1\. ENTER ON CROSS  
>  2\. CHECK RVI if it's past zero then it will be a nice move and i can let it run.. If it isn't past ZERO then i watch the trade carefully  
>  3\. I wait for the price to hit the outer channel (125) then I move to the 5 min TF.. If it retraces by 30 pips i exit the trade.. If it passes the channel i then...

Hi there. Just like to say this is fantastic that minds are coming together to evolve this system, we've had some great suggestions..  
  
Here is something i have been doing to try and determine exits and it looks promising.  
  
ADD the 125 pip trend lines as per previous post.  
ADD 65 pip trend lines  
BOTH to the 100 SMA  
  
And on the 9SMA   
ADD 45 pip and - 45 pip lines to it.  
  
I exit when the 45 pip channel line crosses back over the 100 SMA.

  * [#216](/thread/post/260229#post260229 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 2, 2007 6:24pm  Apr 2, 2007 6:24pm 

  * [ fierceman](fierceman)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Seor Member | [801 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=34680)

Hi guys, seems like a nice system. I use a similar setup, but I prefer to use something a little slower moving than a 9 period SMA, but as in any system, the number of parameter combinations is infinite so at some point you just have to go with your gut. I guess your gut says 9 and who am I to argue with another person's gut?  
  
There are 2 contributions I would like to make:  
1\. Use ADX and other trend indicators along with an eye or two on fundamentals to HELP you determine whether the market is ranging or trending on a longer term. It helps to keep that type of info in the back of your mind.  
  
2\. Instead of using fixed levels at 125, 65, etc, you may want to consider using bollinger bands instead in order to take into account market volatility. Although I think the 125 number is a good one at most times, there are times when using fixed levels becomes inadequate. Try to set the b.band parameters so that you are near that 125 level during "normal" trading volumes/volatility. Watch the bands shrink and adjust exit levels accordingly.  
  
Cheers.

He is tellng you when the 9sma crosses the 100sma after that candle closes thats the entry. You would wait for the close to make sure the cross happens.  
  
you dont enter whe a candle crosses the 100 but when the 9 crossses the 100.  
  
Hope that helps some.   
  
Here is achart showing what a cross entry would look like, the vertical line is on the candle that you would enter on the close of.

hey billser and allanchi..... don't use that ea to trade real money.... it's just an example of a price cross ma version.... again, don't trade with it....  
  
the maximum risk and decreasefactor money management components designed for that purpose....   
  
the _movingperiod_ value in the inputs sets the triggering moving average.... by default it's 10, change that number to your preference.....  
  
that ea is just a simple example for mq4 code study purposes only..... h 

to trade and code, keep both simple... no call to impress....h

  * [#249](/thread/post/262001#post262001 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 4, 2007 6:58am  Apr 4, 2007 6:58am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar1273_4.gif) rockrat](rockrat)

  * | Joined Nov 2004  | Status: Trader | [42 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=1273)

hahaha....... no, thats why i am here.  
i will admit i didnt go in specifically on this MA system as i missed the cross as i already said.  
i did look for a PA indication after to help me get in.  
  
As for exit here are my thoughts to date.  
i think we need to have the two lot entry already mentioned.  
I dont like the 125 levels of the 100MA mentioned as i have found that on several occasions in the past, price has already past this point before the entry signal, this is obviousely when the cross happens when we have a sudden price spike.  
  
Instead i would prefer to take a discretionary exit of the first lot once price has hit 100 pips. This exit would be to look for obvious pivot/resistance TL's etc, and to try an eek out a few additional pips beyond that initial 100 pips.  
  
For the second lot exit, may i suggest that some people far cleverer than i look into the ATR signal indicator, the one currently advocated by team aphids Bat method ( <http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=12808> ) .  
look at the signal on the 1hr chart, and see how the trailing exit has captured pretty much all the maximum pips before price turned.  
i think this is a good possible exit tool to use.  
the trailing exit signal does come some time after the initial entry signal i agree, and maybe that issue can be looked at by somebody better than me.  
  
the other main problem i have yet to overcome with this method is the initial stop. TBWSS says he uses no stop at all, that doesnt sit well with me, but i have been burned so many times by stops on trades that ultimately went in the chosen direction then its obviousley something that i need to work on. 

Its gonna happen, it will happen.....i know!

droesparky,  
  
i see it as no stop as he cant determine what the exit cross would be when it hasnt crossed yet. so when we very first enter the trade, there is currently no stop determined.  
  
As for the ATR, i have looked back and simply considered a break of the trailing signal, so for the current long trade a brek of the blue line yes, i would not even wait for a close below it in my current thinking.  
i have the settings at ATR 5, factor 4.0 and it seems to be pretty good 

Its gonna happen, it will happen.....i know!

  * Apr 4, 2007 2:47pm  Apr 4, 2007 2:47pm 

  * [ tbwss1234](tbwss1234)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: eaglewoodbury | [77 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=35418)

Just to keep you in the loop.. I am attempting to find the simplest and most affective way to exit and also enter avoiding whispaws.  
  
Now i have been looking back at the charts and have found something interesting with an indicator inparticular. This is working with the 9SMA and 100SMA.  
  
Is everyone here familiar with the Ickimoku indicator.. It's great for showing trend direction and range filtering.  
  
If you all set up a   
1\. 30 min CHART  
2\. PAIR GBP/JPY  
3\. Ichimoku Hinko Hyo  
4\. 9SMA and 100 SMA  
  
Now take a look at the Ichimoku indicator particularily the Chinkou Span..  
  
Look at the sell signals for example..  
  
When there is a sell CROSS 9-100SMA when the CHINKOU SPAN is BELOW the price we get a correct entry.. When it is above the price we get a false.. it looks to me it happens just about all the time..   
  
Looks intersting...  
  
OH and for exit.  
  
ON a downtrend when the CHINKOU SPAN Rises above the PRICE we exit the sell and on and uptrend when the CHINKOU SPAN Drops below the price we EXIT.. So the buy at the moment looks like it could be ending..  
  
Take a look guys and see when you think  
  
DO you want me to post a chart? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

Yeah it needs to lag..  
  
When there is distance between the CHINKOU SPAN and the price.. The moves are great..  
  
When the CROSS occurs and the PRICE is Close to The CHINKOU SPAN we need to watch out

dont take this the wrong way, but do your own analysis....you will benefit from it and not rely on somebody elses figures without knowing if they are valid or not.  
turn off autoscroll, close your eyes and pan back a couple of months. Then then use F12 to advance 1 bar at a time and take notes on what you would do and its almost the nearest thing you can get to live trading.   
see how your emotions will affect your decisions when you dont know whats coming up next, then tot up your total pips at the ned of your evaluation. 

Its gonna happen, it will happen.....i know!

  * [#290](/thread/post/265099#post265099 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 7, 2007 2:40am  Apr 7, 2007 2:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar24851_3.gif) hayseed](hayseed)

  * Joined Nov 2006 | Status: Trader | [4,150 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=24851)

hey sparky..... most all ea's will do that ...... if for some reason the ea's author did not include those options, it only takes a second to add them ..... i'll post a few examples from the some of the better coders of the world a little latter....   
  
however, if i could be so bold here..... most all simple ma crossing systems used on small time frames in the forex market will fail in the end...... there is no point denying, when they are hot they are hot but when they are cold......   
  
ma crossovers seem to work better when the higher time frames agree with the lower time frames crossover.... and the agreeing/comfirming higher time frame indicators can be ma's, rsi, stochastic or any such...... think of it like trading the smaller '30 minute' waves on the larger 'weekly' waves..... your still trading the same 30 minute chart as before but only when the larger wave is at your back......h 

to trade and code, keep both simple... no call to impress....h

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar24851_3.gif) hayseed](hayseed)

  * Joined Nov 2006 | Status: Trader | [4,150 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=24851)

hey drayco..... alerts can be added quite quickly to many standard indicators..... or you can just create the alert in a stand alone "heard but not seen" fashion, if say for instance you don't have need or room on your chart for the extra alerting indicator..... in the unseen manner you could have multiple alerts attached to your chart but not cluttering up the works.....   
  
you didn't mention which type you wanted so i added a 0 cross alert to the standard rvi.... set the input 'alert' to 0 to turn off alert..... and the unseen version has no plot.....h  
  
edit...  
combined a ma cross with the rvi.....h  
  
edited yet again...9/7/2007 7:20.... added simple "**untested** " ea version of 9/90 cross with rvi level setting.... all ma variables are adjustable.... rvi threshold is adjustable..... it preforms as one would expect in backtests.... additional supporting indicators are needed before it could be fully trusted with real money.... post any thoughts for improvements......h

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar24851_3.gif) hayseed](hayseed)

  * Joined Nov 2006 | Status: Trader | [4,150 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=24851)

hey sparky..... that's an excellent idea.....   
  
the 0 line will float if the _fixed minimum_ and _fixed maximum_ boxes are not checked and a value inserted when applying the indicator.... +1 and -1 would be the settings in rvi's case.... those settings could be hard coded in the indicator but that can bring on other problems....  
  
as a rule fixed settings are not necessary ...... but if perhaps we want to have the charts time frame _rvi_ and differing time frame using the _mtf rvi indicator_ in the same indicator frame to observe the time frame crossings, we need the 0 solid in place.... this is only an issue when we have 2 differing time frames overlayed ....... otherwise as we scroll forward or backwards the exact point of the 30 minute rvi crossing the 60 minute rvi sometimes will move due to the 0 line floating..... h

hey river..... my preference is for a rvi of 10.... rvi is very similar in shape to stochcastic and stoch(9,5,3) seems fair around.....   
  
i'm not using the method described here in this thread..... my interest is just in tossing a few indicators into the fray...... such as included here..... this is a painted bar indicator in which the bars above the 9/90 cross are lime and below will be red.....   
  
also added 2 arrows for the rvi crossing an adjustable threshold.... default is set to 0...... holler if anything else comes to mind.....h

This looks like a great system even in the ranging markets it's true that profits could be made from what I was noticing it looks like if you were to put a stop about say 25 pips above where the 100 day moving average is that it would not get hit 80% of the time. But i think you would have to enter right on the cross to make sure you catch a positive trade. But as far as the exit strategy maybe a trailing stop could work...

I think this is a good time to test the strength of this system during whipsaws, coz this is what is happening now. On 30m, we had 2 crosses down already, but because RVI is over 0, not a good place to enter.   
  
I think we have to add to this system strong S/R levels and see how the market behaves around them, if it runs or ranges, and this is also how we can avoid whipsaws better.

  * [#328](/thread/post/274777#post274777 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 17, 2007 1:55pm  Apr 17, 2007 1:55pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar36386_8.gif) gagiul](gagiul)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Jacko Trooper | [771 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=36386)

How is everyone trading this strategy?  
  
I try to keep it simple. If 9Sma crosses 100 Sma to the upside, and RVI100 is above 0, I go long. Opposite for short. I also look at the angle of both 9 and 100sma and follow my instincts. Besides this, I am aware of the S/R levels and try not to enter close to one.  
Anyway, during trending periods, this strategy work damn well.   
  
I would like to know how are u people trading using the 125+/- channel.  
  
Thanks. 

We leave no soldier behind.

  * [#332](/thread/post/279793#post279793 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 23, 2007 7:53pm  Apr 23, 2007 7:53pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar36386_8.gif) gagiul](gagiul)

  * | Joined Mar 2007  | Status: Jacko Trooper | [771 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=36386)

well, one way would be to use RVI 100 as a filter. When u get a short cross, check if RVI 100 is under 0 level on a M30 chart. If yes, its quite safe to enter the trade. Same idea for the long.  
  
However, recently it seems that all the good crosses offered a few pips, 50 - 100, then the market reversed completely, so consider also using some TPs. Also, sometimes waiting for the cross can get u in the trade quite late. When u see price crossing down 100 sma and u are sure of a potential sell off, by using oher indicators, jump in and dont wait for the 9sma to cross, because by then the trade may be almost finished. This is rather aggressive approach, but looks like the market is a little choppy these days.  
  
Just my 2 cents. Anyone got other good inputs here? 

We leave no soldier behind.

  * [#338](/thread/post/1425365#post1425365 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 26, 2007 8:19pm  Apr 26, 2007 8:19pm 

  * [ Handelaar](handelaar)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Trader | [4 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=30797)

I have been using the MACD with settings 12,26 and 9 as a filter to this system with great success the last two weeks. I only enter the trade when both indicators (MA's of Eagle Crossover and MACD) points in the same direction. Exit when one of the indicators turns around.   
It seems to keep you out of the market when risky and ensure that you will be in when the big moves in GBP/JPY comes along. When in the market, I log in every hour to see if one of the indicators have perhaps turned and signal an exit.   
Comments will be appreciated. 

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

[![Click to Enlarge

Name: eagle crossover MACD.jpg
Size: 84 KB](/attachment/image/29659/thumbnail?d=1365527861)](/attachment/image/29659?d=1177586356)

  * [#339](/thread/post/1425478#post1425478 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 26, 2007 9:39pm  Apr 26, 2007 9:39pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar33522_4.gif) bundubill](bundubill)

  * | Joined Feb 2007  | Status: bushman | [226 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=33522)

Hi Handelaar  
  
That's interesting. Do you mean you exit if the 9ma starts to turn down even if it's the topside of the 100ma ? And if you do that don't you miss some of the big moves or do you getback in again when it if it turns up ? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#340](/thread/post/1425688#post1425688 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 27, 2007 12:47am  Apr 27, 2007 12:47am 

  * [ Handelaar](handelaar)

  * | Joined Jan 2007  | Status: Trader | [4 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=30797)

Yes Bundubill, the MACD will sometimes require you to exit from a buy when the MA's are still bullish or from a sell when the MA's are still bearish. So yes, you could miss out on some parts of big moves before the MACD prompts you to re-enter. Generally though, the MACD gives the signal to re-enter in time. On the other hand it gives a valuable early warning to exit when the market turns against you.

I trade on the 1 hour timeframe. It might be a good idea to use the 30min just to get in early if the MA's shows a strong trend but overall the 1 hour would suffice and ads the necessary stability.  
I only use the MACD with that particular settings as a filter for the Eagle Crossover System.   
  
Hope this helps.

In my opinion, indicators like STOCH is only good for range bound markets, since it may cause you to enter/exit a trade prematurely for a trending market. The STOCH can only go to 100% and stop there, and though price can continue onward....

> [Quoting bundubill](/thread/post/1427748#post1427748 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> I found this out the hard way yesterday when I decided not to go long on GBP/USD because the stochs showed it was overbought and then watched it go on to make another 90 pips
> 
> Ignored

Oscillators in general are meant for "counter-trend" trades... basically the little peaks and valleys you see in the longer term trend. They work great in sideways markets, but only work in trending markets if you trade with the trend. This is because definitions of "overbought" and "oversold" get thrown out the window when everyone is buying/selling like crazy to give strength to the trend. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * May 8, 2007 10:05pm  May 8, 2007 10:05pm 

  * [ winwise](winwise)

  * | Joined May 2007  | Status: Trader | [154 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=39256)

Thanks for sharing.  
I think if we add momentum into your system, it will much help to spot those long term....big moves!  
"By measuring the amount that a security's price has changed over a given time span, the **Momentum** indicator provides an indication of a market's velocity and to some degree, a measure of the extent to which a trend still holds true. It can also be helpful in spotting likely reversal points.   
  
While the mathematics are straightforward (subtract the closing price _n_ days ago from the closing price today), do not underrate its value because of its simplicity.   
Use the Momentum indicator as a trend-following oscillator similar to the MACD and buy when the indicator bottoms and turns up. Sell when the indicator peaks and turns down. When the Momentum indicator reaches extremely high or low values (relative to historical values) assume a continuation of the current trend. A second usage for the Momentum indicator is as a leading indicator. As a market peaks, the Momentum indicator will climb sharply before falling off. At a market bottom, the plot will drop sharply and then climb well ahead of prices." 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

> "By measuring the amount that a security's price has changed over a given time span, the **Momentum** indicator provides an indication of a market's velocity and to some degree, a measure of the extent to which a trend still holds true. It can also be helpful in spotting likely reversal points.

>  While the mathematics are straightforward (subtract the closing price _n_ days ago from the closing price today), do not underrate its value because of its simplicity.
> 
> Ignored

Co-incidentally, the Momentum indicator is the same thing as the slope of a SMA, but with a different scale. I know some people here like to buy/sell when the slope of an MA changes. For SMAs, this point happens when the Momentum crosses the zero line.  
  
The reason why this works is the middle terms of the SMAs cancel out when you subtract the previous bar's SMA from the current SMA:  
  
SMA of n periods: Sum ( Price (0) ... Price (n-1) ) / n  
SMA(1) of n periods: Sum ( Price (1) ... Price (n) ) / n  
  
Slope of SMA: SMA - SMA(1) = ( Price (0) - Price (n) ) / n  
  
very similar to... Momentum of n periods: Price (0) - Price (n)  
  
Again, the only difference is a matter of scale. If you were to plot the slope of an SMA of n periods on top of a Momentum of n periods and have the charting program automatically rescale the two, they would look exactly the same. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#365](/thread/post/1502610#post1502610 "Post Permalink")

  * Jul 21, 2007 4:39am  Jul 21, 2007 4:39am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar29393_4.gif) Acko](acko)

  * | Membership Revoked  | Joined Dec 2006 | [277 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=29393)

Hi guys  
tbwss1234 and others, I feel, were really onto something and praise should go to those guys.  
Anyway, this is how I use this particular method. Feel free to implement your own measures, but don't muck around with it too much as it's been good to me as it is.  
Remember, this is a method not a system so work with it to suit your personal trading traits. Create your own MM rules, R/R, TP & SL etc...  
There are other good, simple methods on this site e.g., TEB, Cornflower, to name but two and, for me, the best by far is Bagovino's. This forms the basis of my other system. The point being - Simplicity is the key!  
  
Chart - whatever timeframe you want but under 1 hour gives too many whips, higher TFs = bigger moves. Overlay a 100 ema (or 50 if aggressive), this determines the direction we will trade. If price is above we trade long, reverse for shorts.  
  
Entry - overlay an Ichimoku with only Kijun showing set at default, 26 I think.  
Now, if price closes above BOTH lines enter on the high of that bar/candle reverse for shorts. NO moving ave crosses. Waste of time.  
If price is in "the zone", ie,. between the lines then no trade.  
Always check at least one time frame above to determine trend - this is the filter and very important. Trade only in the direction of the higher timeframe trend.  
  
Exit - notice also that the Ichy moves in defined steps. This are my trailing stop positions after hopefully entering profitable territory. Whenever price turns and hits the Ichy I'm out whether in profit or not.   
  
Set conservative profit targets and you should do well.  
  
Thats it. Simple but effective. Please don't ask me for EAs, backtest results and the like. I wouldn't know how, just mastered right clicking! Like I say, play with it and let me know. Try hard to resist adding indicators.  
Dave 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#366](/thread/post/1502815#post1502815 "Post Permalink")

  * Jul 21, 2007 2:40pm  Jul 21, 2007 2:40pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar21271_4.gif) Dreamliner](dreamliner)

  * Joined Oct 2006 | Status: Trader | [2,271 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=21271)

We know that GBP/JPY is a cary trade with huge swap rates, therefore bias will always be long, with occasional corrections. So why not enter long at the cross and exit long at the cross? Short enter at the cross and exit with 50 pips.   
  
This will do 2 things:  
  
First, it will keep you in the long trends, earning a lot of interest and pips at the same time.   
  
Second, it will keep you out of the majority of whip to the short side.  
  
Backtesting this visually on a 4 hour chart (I have a job and can't look more often than 4 hours) over the past years show a very successful method.  
  
I apologize if someone has already posted this as a method for this system. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

T4K  
  
I think you are right about the reason the thread originally died, that and its a crossover method.  
  
I guess even most of the weak months in that data could have been a lot better with some type of exit strat.  
  
alos by the time the method crosses back the opposite directions it has given up a bunch of pips many times.   
  
Exits seem to be the hardest for traders to determine, traders with well defined exits are most likely the better traders.  
  
That said the entry on this system is easy to understand, lets put our heads together and come up with another exit for it.  
  
I do think the cross is one exit that can be left in the system but whatelse is there?

  * | Membership Revoked  | Joined Dec 2006 | [277 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=29393)

Hi bundubill et al  
  
Yeh, exits have always caused me problems in the past, often giving back most if not all and then some. Tricky. One method I've used with some success which may be of assistance is to use a 3ma as a substitute for price (or stay with the 9ema whichever suits) and use 30emas of the highs and lows as exits. The highs as exits when long, lows as exits when short. One can always re-enter, but I look for confirmation from MACD Hist and RSI14 before re-entry. Food for thought!  
  
Hope this helps or at least stimulates the grey matter  
Dave 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * Jul 23, 2007 6:52am  Jul 23, 2007 6:52am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar16397_4.gif) droesparky](droesparky)

  * | Joined Aug 2006  | Status: Trader | [149 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=16397)

maybe a good entry filter would be to only take crosses that are in favor of the higher tf.  
  
say that now on gbp/jpy the 9 is above the 100 on 4hr so we would not take crosses short until the opposite it true. A little lesson from the cornflour system as long as 4h is long we look for lonn opps.  
  
at some point the 4 hr may turn short and we would miss a bunch of pips on the trend change doing this but perhaps if we are watching multi pairs we can always find a pair or two that are crossing in our favor.  
  
this will still leave pips on the table and dosnt solve the exit.  
  
ps not sure how I got that one post all in bold but it was not intentional!

  * Sep 11, 2007 12:35am  Sep 11, 2007 12:35am

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

> [Quoting Dreamliner](/thread/post/1572508#post1572508 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> It is a simple moving average; but surely this 9/100 SMA cross system must have other parameters to it; moving average crosses are no good if used as an "always in" method, going long when cross up happens and short when cross down.  
>    
>  Does anyone know the rest of the system with this 9/100 SMA cross system?
> 
> Ignored

Its pretty much just a MA crossover system. The timeframes for the averages used are designed to avoid <most> but not all whips. It provides easy entries, but exits are harder with this system, that's mostly what has been discussed.  
  
I have seen esp. on higher TFs (daily and weekly) that this system is very effective. Personally, I have this combined with a 28 period Donchian channel which shows me when we are making higher highs and lower lows, and this helps me to exit long moves without waiting for the averages to recross. Of course, it also means I will sometimes get out too early. 

Disregard all prognostications.

  * [#393](/thread/post/1587746#post1587746 "Post Permalink")

  * Sep 12, 2007 5:48am  Sep 12, 2007 5:48am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43318_4.gif) Pidgeon](pidgeon)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

Bundubill,  
  
I wait for the open of the next daily candle. This means I enter most trades in the off hours, between the US session close and the next European session open. This makes it easy to go home and look at forex in the evenings (EST).  
  
Dreamliner,  
  
I'm leaving from work in a few minutes, but tomorrow I'll post a chart that shows how I exit using the Donchian channel. I actually got the indicator from this website, so I want to look up the link to it. It has nice entry indicators for trend following, but that's not how I use it.  
  
Example without the charts...  
I see a 9 / 100 MA cross. I look to see that its going in the general direction of the trend ( using weekly or monthly timeframe ). Then enter on next candle. For exits, I look at the donchian channel indicator to see that we are done making higher highs, and then look for a decent retrace away from the channel ( several day's worth not just one day ) and this provides a good exit signal. This will be before we get another cross of the MAs.  
  
Keep in mind I'm only demoing this strategy for now but I plan to stick with it. I got the idea of using the donchian channel from reading "Trend Following" by Michael Covel. Excellent read btw. 

Disregard all prognostications.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

>  I wait for the open of the next daily candle. This means I enter most trades in the off hours, between the US session close and the next European session open. This makes it easy to go home and look at forex in the evenings (EST).  
>    
>  Dreamliner,  
>    
>  I'm leaving from work in a few minutes, but tomorrow I'll post a chart that shows how I exit using the Donchian channel. I actually got the indicator from this website, so I want to look up the link to it. It has nice entry indicators for trend following, but that's not how I use it.  
>    
>  Example without the charts...  
>  I see a 9 / 100 MA cross. I look to see that its going in the general direction of the trend ( using weekly or monthly timeframe ). Then enter on next candle. For exits, I look at the donchian channel indicator to see that we are done making higher highs, and then look for a decent retrace away from the channel ( several day's worth not just one day ) and this provides a good exit signal. This will be before we get another cross of the MAs.  
>    
>  Keep in mind I'm only demoing this strategy for now but I plan to stick with it. I got the idea of using the donchian channel from reading "Trend Following" by Michael Covel. Excellent read btw.
> 
> Ignored

  * [ Dan](dan)

When I look through history I cant really see any pattern with the RSV.  
If you put an 100 RSI on and then buy or sell only when the 9 MA and 100 Cross and the RSI cross's the 50 level. If the RSI drops below the 50 mark Sell and rises above buy. I would say its good within about 5 or 6 bars prior or after you recieve the MA cross signal.   
  
Ignore all other signals if the RSI hasnt recently crossed the 50 mark and it tends to avoid the false signals.  
  
I havent practiced this yet will start on monday.  
  
I cant see any good exit method yet maybe a 25 trailing stop.

#  [](/thread/22510-eagle-method-ma-crossover-system)Eagle Method MA Crossover System

  * [#401](/thread/post/1811337#post1811337 "Post Permalink")

  * Jan 21, 2008 5:31am  Jan 21, 2008 5:31am 

  * [ gfsound](gfsound)

  * | Joined Apr 2007  | Status: It's hard out there for a pip.... | [28 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=36476)

> [Quoting Dreamliner](/thread/post/1811263#post1811263 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Gfsound,  
>    
>  How exactly do you trade this method? I'm still here, but I think the method died because of not being able to select an acceptable stop loss method.
> 
> Ignored

Yeah, I can see that. I'm just playing with it myself, and what I'm doing is not getting greedy, as there are pips to be had on nearly every trade. I AM missing most of the big runs. I trade g/j smaller TF's (5M) only in direction of higher TF trend (daily, weekly), going for 25 pips, and use the 9 kinda like a T3- if price breaks the 9SMA I'm out (meaning if a candle closes on the other side). That is, if either condition is met I'm out. Not only that but I have the CCI on there just to see if I can't maybe use that. See attached recent trades for example. You'll notice in one of the examples the trend continues after a small retracement, but I'm not going to chase the market around with this system, especially not on the lower TF's.   
  
  
So please don't get me wrong, I'm far from perfecting it (as I just recently stumbled upon this thread and finished reading it), but it seems like there are too many pips to be had with a relatively simple system. As a big fan of KISS, I DON'T want to turn it into a 23 indicator system or anything, but rather a consistent methodology providing small, repeatable profitable trades.   
  
Anyway, it just seemed like the premise has merit and that there are maybe some SL and exit strategies that have yet to be tested. I don't know- maybe I'm wrong but it seems worth working on a little. Any further thoughts or criticisms or ideas are welcome, of course.

  * [#419](/thread/post/3943424#post3943424 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 4:08am  Aug 13, 2010 3:37am | Edited 4:08am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar43318_4.gif) Pidgeon](pidgeon)

  * | Joined Jul 2007  | Status: Seasoned Lurker | [242 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=43318)

Back in 2007 (where did the time go), I posted a reply to this thread, post 390. After trying many other systems (how many of you have used those words heh), I've decided to return to the roots of this one, and TRY to keep to the rules. If you read my prior posts, please know that I'm no longer using Donchian channels with this system, and am trading it on the 1H time frame as the original system was designed.  
  
I will try to help those of you who want to understand the original system. The orig poster is long gone, however he is not the only one to suggest using a large MA / small MA cross, there are plenty of them out there. If we set some ground rules, and then follow them, I think we should do ok.  
  
I've been plagued with trying to make short term trades, and by general over-trading lately. I was even using a 5min system, which I really don't have the time for. Based upon my schedule, I can check my charts two times per day: Once at 7:30am EST (right before open of the US session), and once around 9-10pm EST (end of the day for me.) I can't and won't get up at 3am for the start of the London session, and I don't want to worry about trading in the middle of the work day.  
  
Based on the above however, this system still works quite well. It produces a new signal an average of once every 5-10 days. Here are the rules I will follow. They are pretty much the rules from Post #100 of this thread, with minor modifications. I will explain my entry and exit rules, and will explain how the system prevents trading during ranging periods. I will explain where I place my stop-loss. After that, I'll start trading it with these rules on a small account. Follow along if you like.  
  
  
Moving along then!!  
  
CHART SETUP: (This is for the 1H EUR/USD pair only)  
\------------------------------------------------------  
1\. 9 EMA close / 100 EMA close  
2\. On the 100 MA, add 2 levels of +60 and -60 pips. (In MT4, Click on properties, then click the levels tab of the 100MA).  
3\. Add the RVI indicator (from MT4) with a period of 100.  
4\. Add a level of 0.0 to the RVI indicator.  
  
  
ENTRY RULES:  
1\. Price must start outside of the channel formed by the +60 / -60 levels on the 100 MA.  
2\. Once the 9MA crosses the 100MA, we check the RVI. It must be NEAR zero. I know, "near" is not an absolute term, but it must be pretty damn close. If not, we can sometimes wait a bar or two and it will catch up. If RVI is not near 0, this is likely a whipsaw or ranging market, and we pass up the trade.  
  
STOP LOSS:  
I place my stop on the opposite MA100 "level" from the trade. So, if going long, my stop will be on the bottom level, and if going short, the stop will be on the top level. See the attached chart for illustration. This also has the advantage that the stop can be gradually moved up as the trade progresses. For this pair, I have seen one instance where the stop was taken out at the beginning of the trade. In all other cases, the far level was not touched during the trade.  
  
TAKE PROFIT:  
This is the heart of the entire discussion of the thread. I've decided to keep it extremely simple. I'm going to exit on the next 9/100 MA cross, even if it is not confirmed by RVI. This means that sometimes I will exit a trade and then do nothing until the next signal. I have re-read the entire thread from the beginning, and this seems to be as good a method as any. If you are looking for other ideas for exits, read the thread, there are plenty.  
  
I have attached a chart of the EUR/USD showing the latest signal, and will attach another showing ranging behavior that was filtered out by the rules. Some trades will be stopped out, and some will trigger bad trades even with the rules in place. This is ok, as long as the majority of trades follow the existing trend and stay out of whipsaw markets. I believe you can trade most pairs with this system, but am going to focus only on one for now.  
  
We'll see how things go, and I'll post again when the next signal occurs.

Moving the S/L up would certainly make sense, I'd have it at 2910, just to lock some profits in.

At the moment i am using the 100/9 crossover with MACD for backup.(15m and 30m scalping).  
  
I will be moving back to the longer time frames when we get a bit more volume in the markets in September, but for now i'm grabbing anything from 5 pips to 20 pips on the 15m.

Hi PSmith!  
  
Good to have some company on this thread. I think if you look back a bit, you'll see that MACD was being used as a filter as one of the variants of the system. They were even using Ichmoku in place of the 9MA at some point. Some have also scalped with the system, it works for that too.  
  
I think this system works not because of the crossover itself, but because of the additional requirements to take a cross and trade it. I've seen several crosses already on the Eur/Dollar as well as the Yen/Dollar that didn't meet all the requirements, and have passed on them. Last night, I did take a short on AUD because the cross was valid, and agreed with the 4H trend. That trade is up 47 pips as I write this.  
  
As to the MA alert, thanks for posting that. I usually look at my charts during the day, but I don't place any orders until I get home. This lets me do a little reflection on whether I think the trade will be strong or not. Lately we've had a lot of August sideways movement. 

Disregard all prognostications.
